  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_01d47dc9-5b33-4ec4-8ab4-e15ab927cb6e'
      });

<div id="review_859353174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859353174" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/859353174?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer859353174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9843021038590430210">I'd read a couple of sniffy reviews about this book and a friend was very meh about it ... even Weeks himself seemed a touch apologetic about his debut when he saw my tweet about starting it ... though I could be over-reading 140 characters there. In any event, my expectations were not sky high.<br/><br/>It turns out that I tend to like what people tend to like ... who knew? I don't enjoy every popular book but I do generally find out that there's a good reason why they're popular. <br/><br/>Brent Weeks is a great </span>
  <span id="freeText9843021038590430210" style="display:none">I'd read a couple of sniffy reviews about this book and a friend was very meh about it ... even Weeks himself seemed a touch apologetic about his debut when he saw my tweet about starting it ... though I could be over-reading 140 characters there. In any event, my expectations were not sky high.<br /><br />It turns out that I tend to like what people tend to like ... who knew? I don't enjoy every popular book but I do generally find out that there's a good reason why they're popular. <br /><br />Brent Weeks is a great story teller and his writing is plenty strong enough to carry the load. I call the book fun, and it is, but that's not to diminish it in any way. There are plenty of emotional scenes and even though I could see the strings being pulled, I still got drawn in. There's as much action as any reader could want, varied and interesting magic, tight plotting from a good number of interesting points of view. The pacing is good and there are few info dumps. I could perhaps have stood fewer discussions on the city's varied architecture but that's the very minor niggle on the back of a great deal of enjoyment.<br /><br />And that friend of mine who wasn't a fan - she wasn't a fan of The Warded Man either, which I loved, and I have to say that this is probably the most enjoyable read I've had since devouring Brett's The Warded Man several years ago. Like that book TWoS takes what I loved about 80's fantasy and grows it up for the more demanding, hard-edged tastes of today. Definitely recommended.<br /><br />Perhaps the book benefited from me having a rare day to myself and reading most of it in one go. Then again I could have done a lot of other things with that day ... and Weeks' story didn't let me!<br /><br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br />......</span>
  <a data-text-id="9843021038590430210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_310693394" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310693394" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310693394?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of videogame-style fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nataliya by: </span>
      GR positive reviews
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310693394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7862857754037918482">A plucky street urchin Azoth wants to be a <b>wetboy</b> (*). Which is basically an <b>
  <i>assassin on steroids</i>
</b>. Minus the unfortunate side effects of acne, neck hump, obesity, testicular atrophy, and man-boobs. <blockquote>Also, call me immature, but when you call your magical artifact <i>ka'kari</i>, despite the mandatory fantasy apostrophe, the "kaka" part inevitably elicits immature giggles from me. <b>Dear writers, please be careful in your word choices.</b> </blockquote> Anyway, as I said above, our plucky street urchin (hello, fantasy t</span>
  <span id="freeText7862857754037918482" style="display:none">A plucky street urchin Azoth wants to be a <b>wetboy</b> (*). Which is basically an <b>
  <i>assassin on steroids</i>
</b>. Minus the unfortunate side effects of acne, neck hump, obesity, testicular atrophy, and man-boobs. <blockquote>Also, call me immature, but when you call your magical artifact <i>ka'kari</i>, despite the mandatory fantasy apostrophe, the "kaka" part inevitably elicits immature giggles from me. <b>Dear writers, please be careful in your word choices.</b> </blockquote> Anyway, as I said above, our plucky street urchin (hello, fantasy trope!) Azoth strives to become a super-assassin under the tutelage of Durzo Blint, a cruel badass wetboy (<b>
  <i>but deep, deep, deeeeeeep down inside he is, of course, a caring mentor in his own gruffy way - hello, another trope!</i>
</b>). He gets his wish after a few counts of child rape and child mutilation - but relax, it does not happen to Azoth; <i>
  <b>really bad things are only allowed to happen to the sidekicks</b>
</i>. Anyway, he gets the training and adopts the identity of <b>Kylar Stern,</b> which sounds marginally better than Azoth. <blockquote>
  <i>"The truth was, Azoth hated Azoth. Azoth was a coward, passive, weak, afraid, disloyal. Azoth had hesitated [...] He was Kylar now, and Kylar would be everything Azoth hadn’t dared to be."</i>
</blockquote>He meets a <b>noble and honorable Logan</b> along the way (<i>to be prominently featured in the sequels</i>). He also has a mandatory love interest - <b>a saintly mind-numbingly boring Elene</b>, whose soul is pure and childhood disfigurement does not seem to interfere with her beauty, like, at all. <b>She basically is a virginal Madonna of this story.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380374804i/729084.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>NO, NOT <b>
  <u>THAT</u>
</b> MADONNA.................<b>
  <u>THIS</u>
</b> ONE!<br><br>One of my main gripes with this story is <b>the overreliance on fantasy tropes/cliches</b>. In this case, in addition to the ones above, we get a mandatory <b>virgin-whore dichotomy</b> (Elene being the virgin). And another trope - pretty much all the whores turn out to have <b>a heart of gold</b>. Of course. <br><br>*****<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380370206i/723009.jpg" width="330" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">****<br><i>No, really, women come in more than two varieties. Believe me.</i><br><br>The character development of the entire story is rather non-existent, more of a videogame variety. <b>The characters are cardboard caricatures</b> - very perfunctory, very stereotypical and cliched, with very little stepping out of of designed fantasy tropes. Durzo Blint failed to arouse much sympathy or admiration despite learning about his tragic/tortured backstory. Logan is a prototypical hero/good guy. Elene is a cute love interest devoid of personality. Only Jarl and Momma K seemed to be interesting at all, but they don't get nearly enough on-page time. As for Azoth/Kylar himself, he is a decent action hero, but I could not care less for him as a person; he just lacks depth.<br><br>Nevertheless, despite characterization being his weak point, Weeks is a good storyteller. His story is very plot-driven and flows reasonably well with the exception of a few parts where the pacing was a bit uneven. The plot drags just a bit in the first part, but picks up quite nicely in the second half of the book. <b>Action scenes are vivid and written very well, and the loose ends get nicely wrapped up.</b> The book, despite its weaknesses, managed to eventually capture my attention, making it hard to put down until I got to the end. <i>
  <b>Reading it is, in my limited experience, just like playing a videogame - a fun ride without too much depth.</b>
</i><br><br>-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br><b>Overall, an average <s>3-star</s> 2-star¹ story with forgettable characters, overreliance on fantasy cliches, and the feel of a videogame put to page, but rather fun and with nice action scenes.</b> Nothing special, but it got me interested enough to pick up the sequel. Brent Weeks does show promise as a writer, especially if he eventually steps outside the familiar and comfortable fantasy genre patterns.<blockquote>¹ After realizing that I have given 3 stars to quite a few books that I liked way more than this one, I realized that the fair thing to do would be to knock this one down a star. For the life of me, I have no idea why I was so generous with rating it in the first place.</blockquote></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1602908935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602908935" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1602908935?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=priority-2017">priority-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=grimdark">grimdark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602908935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10652725860881027614"><b>1.5/5</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Do you know what punishments I've endured for my crimes, my sins?" </i>
</b><i> <- I read The Way of Shadows by Brent Weeks, I think that's punishment enough for my sins.</i><br/><br/>This novel had a promising start, I really enjoyed the start and was excited to fangirl over this novel for eternity, as everyone already knows I am Brent Weeks trash & I'm not ashamed to admit it. So I expected to absolutely adore this book, to be submerged in feels and just want to cuddle it for long hours and cry tears of adora</span>
  <span id="freeText10652725860881027614" style="display:none"><b>1.5/5</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Do you know what punishments I've endured for my crimes, my sins?" </i>
</b><i> &lt;- I read The Way of Shadows by Brent Weeks, I think that's punishment enough for my sins.</i><br /><br />This novel had a promising start, I really enjoyed the start and was excited to fangirl over this novel for eternity, as everyone already knows I am Brent Weeks trash &amp; I'm not ashamed to admit it. So I expected to absolutely adore this book, to be submerged in feels and just want to cuddle it for long hours and cry tears of adoration. Having a promising start and being quite fun I thought I'd hit the lottery. It starts off with some Locke Lamorr vibes, a bunch of young children living in a guild. A tiny 9 year old girl gets cut up for fun and a young boy is raped into submission. Extremely grim and totally had my full attention, however it quickly went sour from there and I lost interest very fast and after a while I realised I hadn't hit the lottery at all and what I instead had was a cliche novel full of tropes, sucky names and forced badassery. Lets be honest here folks the writing was extremely choppy and lacked direction, most of the story itself was talking and talking is boring. I wanted a lot more show instead of tell. But weeks only delivered 5% show the rest was just lines of whining and a POV from an insecure child... sound familiar? Kylar (Azroth) is a twin of Kip (lightbringer series) except it's not "I'm so fat" instead it is "I can't protect those I love.. Wah Wah Wah". I don't know if it's a case of its me and not you Brent Weeks, or it's a full blown case of it was definitely Brent Weeks fault why I disliked this novel so much and can't continue with this series because it's the same old crap from his other series and I can't be bothered reading garbage. Maybe I've just out grown Brent Weeks stupid horny school boy writing style? I'm not sure. I honestly hope not tho... <b>because I am and always will be Gavin Guile (lightbringer series) trash. </b>Another major issue I had with the novel is the use of the word "Wetboy" for an assassin name.. shittest assassin name ever... like ever.. How could someone even justify calling a killer such a pathetically shit name? I'm not even kidding right now, anything would have been better and tougher then that name. I can think of atleast 7 names which would have been cooler and more appropriate. When I think of a Wetboy I think of something a pedophile would google or that awkward moment after my toddlers bath and I chase him around the house with a towel screaming "get here boy, your wet".<br /><br />So this book is marketed as "grimdark" or "dark fantasy" WHICH ACTUALLY RUFFLES MY FEATHERS. What a load of dog shit.. About two things in this novel could be considered grim &amp; both happened in the first 100 pages. The main character is an assassin who ONLY KILLS BAD PEOPLE. WHICH THEREFOR MAKES HIM A HERO. He is not a grey character but instead pure white. <b>“It is better to suffer evil than to do evil.”</b> are you sure about that? Pretty sure only evil people become assassins but anyway.. you go be white and a hero Kylar, no one gives a fuck. I'm so bored of your standard black/white characters, they honestly have no depth or personality and I'm not interested in heroes, they are boring. <b>But my main problem with this book is the lack of originality and the fact it stunk so badly of this authors other series that I can't even forgive this for being a debut novel, </b>Brent has brought nothing new to the fantasy genre or his own writing style. It was actually pretty childish and kinda lame. Are we certain this series wasn't written by Brent at age 12? When he first hit puberty and could only think about sex, girls and wanking?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Life is empty. Life is meaningless. When we take a life, we arn't taking anything of value. Wetboys are killers. Thats all we do. Thats all we are. There are no poets in the bitter business.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />The story is basically about a child named Azroth who wants to become an assassin so he can stand up to his bullies in the guild and protect his friends. One night he runs into Durzo Blint the baddest and deadliest assassin going around. Durzo doesn't take on apprentices so it's Azroths job to impress him and show Durzo why he should be apprenticed. After awhile Azroths changes his name to Kylar Stern and to be honest the book gets more and more cliched towards the ending. Don't get me wrong, I'm a sucker for a well done cliche plot; I love assassins, I love magic, I love the hateful but nice mentor, I love the weak boy who turns into a strong focused individual trope.. What can I say I just love tropes, however this book just made me roll my eyes, it was boring, annoying, I honestly felt like I had read this book 1000 times over. It's safe to say I'm actually sick of these tropes, this was not a warm trope cuddle more of a trope slap. But it wasn't all bad there was a few redeeming factors; some of the twists and plot points were unpredictable and made the story more interesting, the magic system was interesting, Durzo Blint was cool... Ummm.. *cough*.. Hmm let me think.. That's literally all I can think of... So yeah pretty much a bust.<br /><br />Recommended to people looking for a novel to begin with in the adult fantasy genre. <br /><br /><b>Ps. Safe to say I will not read the rest of the series because quite frankly I got better things to do. 😴😴</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10652725860881027614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_901748643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/901748643" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/901748643?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6070107-the-way-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901748643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16572033410623308521"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>”I don’t ask you to like reality. I only ask you to be strong enough to face it.”</i><br/><br/>Durzo Blint is Cenaria’s most feared killer. Azoth is a frightened little boy living on the streets. Through a series of coincidences, the two come together in the dark underworld of the capital, and the guild rat becomes the assassin’s apprentice.<br/><br/>The only thing you know about the plot is that you’re following Azoth’s journey from the streets to becoming a top-notch killer. That can make things a bit confus</span>
  <span id="freeText16572033410623308521" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><i>”I don’t ask you to like reality. I only ask you to be strong enough to face it.”</i><br><br>Durzo Blint is Cenaria’s most feared killer. Azoth is a frightened little boy living on the streets. Through a series of coincidences, the two come together in the dark underworld of the capital, and the guild rat becomes the assassin’s apprentice.<br><br>The only thing you know about the plot is that you’re following Azoth’s journey from the streets to becoming a top-notch killer. That can make things a bit confusing, as you’ll occasionally wonder what on earth is actually going on, but at least it’s mostly coherent. And luckily, there are tons of interesting subplots coming up every now and then.<br><br>The setting is interesting enough, but not in such a way that it adds to the overall quality of the book. It’s a city; a capital city, and the novel takes place on its streets and in its mansions and castles. As for the world, it does appear to have many interesting aspects, but sometimes it feels as if though random lore is added to give depth where there is none. However, as fantasy lore is like a drug to me, I won’t pretend to dislike it.<br><br>Azoth himself is generic young human male protagonist #1162. There is nothing special about him, his personality, or the way he does anything. <i>However</i>, this is actually positive for the book, as it takes away the attention from him, and sets the focus on the book’s absodamnlutely fabulous secondary characters.<br><br>Just like in many other books, movies and games, <i>The Way of Shadows</i> is about a mentor-protegé relationship where the obvious star of the show is the mentor. Durzo Blint is the most skilled and infamous killer in Cenaria, and by far the character with the most depth. He’s the one with all the secrets and the mysterious past. The one everyone fears, to the extent that he may insult the king with virtual impunity. And does so repeatedly…<br><br><i>“Your Majesty,” Durzo said gravely. “A man of your stature’s cursing vocabulary ought to extend beyond a tedious reiteration of the excreta that fills the void between his ears.”</i><br><br>Aside from Durzo, there is a trio of incredibly interesting noblemen who steal the show from time to time. The first, Duke Regnus Gyre, is the good noble archetype. The one who refuses to seize the throne because it would be dishonourable, and walks knowingly into exile instead. Gyre is a great character to read about, but it is the other two who really caught my attention.<br><br>The curious thing is that both of these characters became my favourites in an instant. In one scene. In the case of Count Drake, that instant was in the middle of a short conversation where he talks about his past, which is, if possible, even more interesting than Durzo’s.<br><br>But the other… oooh, my. Lord General Agon, ladies and gentlemen. Lord General Brant Agon, with a single swift swing of his sword, became my favourite literary character of all the ones I’ve encountered this year.<br><br>On the other hand, there is also another character, who goes by the name of Elene, who is so incomprehensibly annoying I would say she’s singlehandedly responsible for much of my disappointment with the book. I don’t really want to talk about her.<br><br>As for the writing, this is not a book in which to search for eloquence or beautiful prose. Weeks’ style is the same simplistic one that has been popularised by several of the most rapidly rising stars in fantasy in recent years. The best word to describe it is <i>adequate</i>. It does not add anything to the quality of the book, but it serves its purpose.<br><br>There is one major downside, however, and that’s the fact I have never read a fantasy book with a more stupid terminology. Durzo Blint is a <i>wetboy</i>, and while that sounds like an orphaned kid running the streets doing shit jobs for change money, the book gives the notion that a wetboy is some sort of ridiculously super-skilled master-assassin. The only thing that’s even more ridiculous is when the characters are trying to figure out what a female wetboy is called.<br><br>The book is not so fast-paced in the beginning, but eventually it gets unputdownable. The last twenty or thirty chapters are filled with deadly action and fascinating revelations to no end. And while I was disappointed by the ending itself, I would say that the second half of the book as a whole was great.<br><br>So as a whole, <i>The Way of Shadows</i> is not a disappointing book, but it’s not impressive either. There is nothing that will blow your mind away, but there is plenty of excitement. It’s a flawed book kicking off an interesting series, and so I am definitely interested in learning what happens in the continuation of Azoth’s journeys.<br><br><b>
  <i>”Now, boy, are you ready to become a sword in the shadows?”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440713010i/16013362._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16572033410623308521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5290185588711054065">*New individual reviews are on the way. Until then, make your self comfortable with this sorry excuse of a review" <br/><br/><br/>This review is for the whole series (spoiler free).<br/>This is, by far, my favorite fantasy story of all times. It begins as a personal story of a kid apprenticed to an Assassin, and ends as an EPIC fantasy story, including amazing magic, mystical artifacts, Immortals, Godkings, and of course politics. <br/><br/>Both character & world building are impressive (Its architecture is delicate and refi</span>
  <span id="freeText5290185588711054065" style="display:none">*New individual reviews are on the way. Until then, make your self comfortable with this sorry excuse of a review" <br /><br /><br />This review is for the whole series (spoiler free).<br />This is, by far, my favorite fantasy story of all times. It begins as a personal story of a kid apprenticed to an Assassin, and ends as an EPIC fantasy story, including amazing magic, mystical artifacts, Immortals, Godkings, and of course politics. <br /><br />Both character &amp; world building are impressive (Its architecture is delicate and refined), but the gem of this book is the magic system. Magic easy to understand, yet complex and multi-leveled. The pace in all of the books is great, except perhaps the first 100 pages of The Way of Shadows. <br /><br />"That pain you feel," Master Blint said almost gently, "is the pain of abandoning a delusion. The delusion is meaning, Kylar. There is no higher purpose. There are no gods. No arbiters of right and wrong. I don't ask you to like reality. I only ask you to be strong enough to face it. There is nothing beyond this. There is only the perfection we attain by becoming weapons, as strong and merciless as a sword. There is no essential good in living. Life is nothing in itself. It's a place marker that proves who's winning, and we are the winners. We are always the winners. There is nothing by the winning. Even winning means nothing. We win because it's an insult to lose. The ends don't justify the means. The means don't justify the ends. There is no one to justify to. There is no justification."<br /><br />Finally, in this book, you will meet the biggest bad mofo* of Fantasy. Forget Logen Ninefingers. Forget Jorg of Ancrath. Forget Vaelin al Sorna &amp; Kvothe. Here you will get to learn Durzo -fucking- Blint. I totally recommend this book to every fantasy reader out there, and trust me, you will love it!<br /><br />*bad mofo: A person of such dangerous capability that it produces a natural coolness about them, which when those two qualities combine (coolness and danger) create a reputation that is renowned. They exude these qualities in every aspect of day to day living, therefore leaving their mark on society in legendary form. Other Synonyms: Durzo Blint, Acaleus Thorn, Dehvirahaman ko Bruhmaeziwakazari<br /><br />You can find more of my reviews over at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://BookNest.eu/">http://BookNest.eu/</a> </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_950065377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950065377" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950065377?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950065377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8111030231106549948">If Charles Dickens was born in 1977 and grew up playing Dungeons and Dragons and then World of Warcraft and reading sword and sorcery mags and playing online games and who liked wearing a cowled hoody all the time – he may have come up with a book much like Brent Weeks’ The Way of Shadows.<br/><br/>This is a good book. <br/><br/>I was prepared to dislike it, thinking that it would be a pulpy X Box serialization or a campy Assassin’s Creed type fantasy – and both descriptions are fairly accurate – but it is also muc</span>
  <span id="freeText8111030231106549948" style="display:none">If Charles Dickens was born in 1977 and grew up playing Dungeons and Dragons and then World of Warcraft and reading sword and sorcery mags and playing online games and who liked wearing a cowled hoody all the time – he may have come up with a book much like Brent Weeks’ The Way of Shadows.<br><br>This is a good book. <br><br>I was prepared to dislike it, thinking that it would be a pulpy X Box serialization or a campy Assassin’s Creed type fantasy – and both descriptions are fairly accurate – but it is also much more.<br><br>Actually, this is a gritty, bloody book. The subject matter is, after all, a bildungsroman about an assassin, ahem – a WETBOY. Weeks’ does an above average job with characterization and the plot is none too sophomoric. There is more than enough to keep a reader engaged throughout the 600 plus pages. Weeks writes about good and evil, right and wrong with the odd perspective shared with Michael Moorcock’s Elric saga, coming from the outside looking in. Or with a nod to Piers Anthony’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76664.A_Spell_for_Chameleon__Xanth__1_" title="A Spell for Chameleon (Xanth #1) by Piers Anthony" rel="nofollow noopener">A Spell for Chameleon</a>.<br><br>This is not great literature, but it is a lot of fun. Weeks is a great writer in much the same way as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/823561.I__the_Jury__Mike_Hammer___1_" title="I, the Jury (Mike Hammer, #1) by Mickey Spillane" rel="nofollow noopener">I, the Jury</a> is a great book and Mickey Spillane a great writer (as opposed to Hemingway being an Author). Actually, this is great in the same way that Bruce Lee’s Enter the Dragon is great. <br><br>Enter the Dragon was never going to win an Academy Award, but it did get a ton of respect and street cred. Why? Because it does what it does very well. A reader picking up Way of Shadows or a viewer selecting Enter the Dragon likely does not care why Heathcliff loves Cathy, or why The English Patient was a cinematic success. What this reader or viewer does care about is that Weeks delivers a damn fine adventure. Charles Dickens or Mickey Spillane (or Bruce Lee) would be proud.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496316505i/22900073._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8111030231106549948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=video-game-fantasy">video-game-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177674220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16637628438664436597">Likeable, really, but something made this a hard book to delve into and get lost in the story. Could be the gritty scrabble of life in the mud of the Warrens. Could be that while character building was excellent, the world outside the Warrens lacks details, even as we meet the characters living there. Could be I've read too many stories lately with heroes of questionable ethics, and I need to cleanse my palate with light and fluffy (taking applications for light and fluffy~).<br/><br/>Halfway through. Fou</span>
  <span id="freeText16637628438664436597" style="display:none">Likeable, really, but something made this a hard book to delve into and get lost in the story. Could be the gritty scrabble of life in the mud of the Warrens. Could be that while character building was excellent, the world outside the Warrens lacks details, even as we meet the characters living there. Could be I've read too many stories lately with heroes of questionable ethics, and I need to cleanse my palate with light and fluffy (taking applications for light and fluffy~).<br /><br />Halfway through. Found myself starting to skim to get to the resolution (or get to bed; sometimes they coincide), so I put it down until I could focus. I'm finally liking the world being created. The characters are interesting, and the narrative has returned to each enough times that I care at least a little bit about them, and if a few are rather one-dimensional (especially the love interest), overall they are done well.<br /><br />I do find that there seems to be awkward narrative jumps, where one moment we are going through a day per chapter, and then all of a sudden, <i> movie montage</i> our character is sixteen, almost completely transformed from the awkward, unskilled youth into a fully competent assassin. Additionally, the narrative skips around, from primary to characters so minor that they are never heard from again--insert carol's lament of the disjointed narrative standing in for foreshadowing and tension-building--<br /><br />Almost finished. Surprised by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the fact that Kylar was allowed to read Eileen's letters, and didn't leave them hanging. Also surprised that Jarl made a reappearance and had advanced basically parallel to Kylar without Kylar knowing it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The overall political maneuvering is fairly clear and understandable, and the plot did have a couple of twists that left me surprised.<br /><br />Conclusion? Good enough to lure me to the second book, but not enough to join my library.<br /><br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/05/19/the-way-of-shadows-by-brent-weeks/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_90574945" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90574945" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90574945?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90574945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13037630927717353632">There are a few authors, Joe Abercrombie included, whose books I've read in large part because everything they've said outside of their novels (on blogs, etc.) has been hilarious and witty and they don't take themselves too seriously. Brent Weeks (or Sussex Months...yes I still think it's funny) is one of those authors.<br/><br/>One of the reasons it's taken me this long to get to this book is because I think the cover is awful. I know cover art doesn't really effect anything and probably shouldn't anyway</span>
  <span id="freeText13037630927717353632" style="display:none">There are a few authors, Joe Abercrombie included, whose books I've read in large part because everything they've said outside of their novels (on blogs, etc.) has been hilarious and witty and they don't take themselves too seriously. Brent Weeks (or Sussex Months...yes I still think it's funny) is one of those authors.<br /><br />One of the reasons it's taken me this long to get to this book is because I think the cover is awful. I know cover art doesn't really effect anything and probably shouldn't anyway, but it was very off-putting for me. Does anyone really want to see Hayden Christensen dressed up for Halloween on a cover? Maybe I shouldn't ask that... :) (It does look like HC doesn't it?)<br /><br />The covers were what set this series apart, although it's hard to imagine that now, but they set the standard that is now almost a necessity and I can at least give them credit for doing that much. But really, what would a fantasy novel cover be without a cowled figure anyway...original?<br /><br />Okay, now that the cheap shots are out of the way. I do love a good hood and The Way of Shadows (2008, 645 pp.) is full of them. Realistic covers, for me though, only really work for urban fantasy/paranormal romance. It must be the tats I guess. :)<br /><br />This tale begins with the struggles of our main protagonist, Azoth, a guild rat - a nothing who's got no where to go and nothing to lose. His only way to escape the slums and a life of cruelty and pain is to apprentice himself to Durzo Blint, a renowned wetboy (kinda like an assassin times a hundred) and legend. This, however, is not as easy as he supposed since he is forced to turn his back on anyone he's ever loved and devote himself to a practice that's not altogether savory for anyone with some sense of morals. Like the cover blurb says, "The perfect killer has no friends - only targets."<br /><br />To accomplish this, Azoth is given a new identity and a new name, Kylar Stern, while he begins his training and attempts to unleash his "Talent", or his magical abilities that would extend his skills as a wetboy.<br /><br />The Way of Shadows is a fast-paced dynamite of a novel. I was up late into the night burning through pages to find out the next twist. I have to admit, I love a good assassin-themed novel. Weeks does a great job with characterization and I became really attached to Kylar, Momma K, and Logan; some awesome characters with convincing motives. This is the definite focus over world-building, which while an admirably realized world, is only given the barest of details necessary to further the plot. In a character/plot driven novel, The Way of Shadows doesn't get bogged down in description and it was much appreciated.<br /><br />Kylar, although desiring to be a killer, is easy to relate to and has his own qualms throughout the story of doing such work. His character works well with his cranky master, Durzo Blint, who seems to have given up any such feelings of regret for his job. And, although this story plays on many fantasy archetypes (assassins, masters, a powerful sword, an unconquerable enemy), Weeks creates a unique feel that is all his own.<br /><br />One thing I was surprised about was how violent The Way of Shadows is. For some reason, it was not what I was expecting (weird - assassins = violent?), leaning more toward The First Law trilogy than anything. I'm not complaining, it was only unexpected. Weeks does a good job weaving it into the story adding to the emotions (mostly of hatred toward the inflicter) the reader feels for the characters.<br /><br />Basic grammar errors, such as missing words, were almost to the point of annoyance, but didn't distract too much from the story and in the end I felt that the climax was a little underwhelming as I didn't feel like the actions of the main characters were as necessary as they were made out to be. Otherwise The Way of Shadows was romping good fun. I didn't realize I would like this series so much.<br /><br />When Should You Read The Way of Shadows?<br /><br />The best time to read The Way of Shadows is when you're in the mood for something action-packed and quick-paced. If you need a break from reading description after description and you want something that moves the plot forward through short, concise chapters, The Way of Shadows will do you good.<br /><br />And in the end, covers don't really matter as long as the book's good.<br /><br />(side note: I may sound like I hate descriptive novels, but this is far from the truth. I do like balance, however, and a frequent mix of faster and slower novels fit the bill for me.)<br /><br />Rating and Links<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (Really really liked it)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13037630927717353632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_552100234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/552100234" />
    <a title="Andrew Obrigewitsch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16087568-andrew-obrigewitsch"><img alt="Andrew Obrigewitsch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512627613p2/16087568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/552100234?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Obrigewitsch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Obrigewitsch" href="/user/show/16087568-andrew-obrigewitsch">Andrew Obrigewitsch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400112869" href="/book/show/7008432-the-way-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16087568-andrew-obrigewitsch?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552100234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11341973257512453755">I found this series to have the kind of "well" written and "witty" dialogue that every 12 year old pervert will love, due to its "well" thought out and "intellectual" nature. However, I beseech one to read this series as one will not be surprised in the least by the plot twists. In fact from page one, a discernible reader will know the basic ending of the story, and thus can praise it for being a well written work of fantasy. <br/><br/>The author's characterization of women as being either virgins or whor</span>
  <span id="freeText11341973257512453755" style="display:none">I found this series to have the kind of "well" written and "witty" dialogue that every 12 year old pervert will love, due to its "well" thought out and "intellectual" nature. However, I beseech one to read this series as one will not be surprised in the least by the plot twists. In fact from page one, a discernible reader will know the basic ending of the story, and thus can praise it for being a well written work of fantasy. <br /><br />The author's characterization of women as being either virgins or whores will astound even the most ignoble character. And one can only marvel at the rate which the lesser characters die off, while the major ones do not. <br /><br />Seriously though, all I can say is WOW!<br /><br />This was the MOST overhyped book I have ever read. So many people recommended it to me I expected something really good. What I got was a book that felt like a young adult book that was trying to be adult by swearing and talking about sex, just like a 12 year old boy would do.<br /><br />While the book was entertaining and had some good concepts, it was deeply flawed in many ways, and really felt like it was targeted to 12-20 year old crowd, or should have been a CW network TV show. It was full of overused tropes and the way side characters all died off was like watching horror movie were everyone gets killed really easily while the hero can miraculously survive. And lastly there were many similarities in this book to the first book of the Mistborn Series, only the Mistborn book was, way, way better. <br /><br />Now given that this was the author's first book I will cut him some slack and say that the battle scenes were well done and the way magic was used was cool, if not fully explained with rules applied. I will check out the next book to see if the writing improves (which I heard it does, but from what I heard this was one of the best books ever written too, so what I heard my also be false) and the overall plot does get your interest, the machinations of foreign powers taking over. <br /><br />For people who have not read The Broken Sword by Paul Anderson, The Black Company, Fritz Leiber, The Chronicles of Amber, Robin Hob's Assassin novel, or the Deed of Paksenarrion by Elizabeth Moon, I recommend all those over this. And if you want a long read, then Game of Thrones and Wheels of Time are both better as well. Unless you are in your late teens or early 20's, then you will probably love this story. <br /><br />I have had a couple of grammar "experts", come on here and tell me I'm using quotation marks incorrectly. So let me tell you that quotation marks can be used to show sarcasm, it is actually a standard use of them, but don't take my word for it go to the link below:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://grammar.yourdictionary.com/punctuation/how/how-to-use-quotation-marks.html">http://grammar.yourdictionary.com/pun...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11341973257512453755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2276407284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2276407284" />
    <a title="Dana Ilie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie"><img alt="Dana Ilie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584606424p2/21690081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2276407284?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2276407284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8631316061140726492">Brent Weeks has done a great job of tying it all together. While Azoth is the main character, several other plot strands with different characters are introduced and expertly tied together further down the line.<br/><br/>This was one of those books that once I started I couldn’t put down – well written and with a strong story to boot, I’m looking forward to checking out the rest of the trilogy.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933854898?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933854898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer473412218865810392"><b>Since this book is full of tropes and stereotypes I'm going to do this review Disney style!</b><br/><br/>Our main character Azoth is a street urchin. <i>Don't you love street urchins?</i> Of course you do! You have been conditioned by Disney to do so. (Remember Lady and the Tramp? Aristocats? Aladdin?!)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446223882i/16767347._SX540_.jpg' width='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Azoth meets Durzo, a <s>master assassin</s>, sorry, master Wetboy. And here comes my first problem with this book. <b>I HATE the word 'wetboy'.</b> I always thought it was silly how some people hate the word 'moist'… until I read t</span>
  <span id="freeText473412218865810392" style="display:none"><b>Since this book is full of tropes and stereotypes I'm going to do this review Disney style!</b><br><br>Our main character Azoth is a street urchin. <i>Don't you love street urchins?</i> Of course you do! You have been conditioned by Disney to do so. (Remember Lady and the Tramp? Aristocats? Aladdin?!)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446223882i/16767347._SX540_.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Azoth meets Durzo, a <s>master assassin</s>, sorry, master Wetboy. And here comes my first problem with this book. <b>I HATE the word 'wetboy'.</b> I always thought it was silly how some people hate the word 'moist'… until I read the word 'wetboy'. Every time Durzo says they're better than assassins I just shake my head sadly. <br><br>From there the book follows a typical master-apprentice pattern.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446223882i/16767348._SX540_.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Including the required growing up montage à la Lion King.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446224522i/16767373._SX540_.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Azoth (now called Kylar) is a full assassin (I refuse to call him a wetboy) and the book has all the required fantasy characters, including the love interest and main reason I hated this book: Elene. <br><br>Elene was a friend of Kylar from his street urchin days, she was attacked and disfigured, and Kylar blames himself. But never mind the scars, because she's lovely, not just lovely but beautiful! Gorgeous!!! Her whole characterization is a string of synonyms of the word beauty (I'm surprised he didn't call her Belle) Oh, and she's a saint, there's no better girl in the whole world *rolls eyes* <br><br>Since we're doing this Disney style, Elene is going to be the prince from Snow White. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446223683i/16767335._SX540_.png" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Do you remember anything about him? <br><br>Of course not. He’s a freaking placeholder. Just like Elene. And Kylar is totally obsessed with her. I refuse to call that love. :/<br><br>Then we have some battles and some pretty good twists, sadly I read this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/theRevanchist" rel="nofollow noopener">Markus</a>, who was always coming up with possible plots and ideas that sometimes ended up being more interesting than what actually happened in the book!<br><br><b>Do I recommend this?</b> Maybe if you like Assassins and convoluted plots? <br><br><b>Will I read the next one?</b> Nope. I’ll write my reasons on a review for that later. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4167090350452240387">So this book was a pleasant surprise! I left for New York and had only packed one book, thinking I wouldn't be able to read the entire book on my trip...oops. So I had to run to the bookstore to pick out another book to read. The bookstore closed in five minuets and I quickly grabbed the book because of it's interesting looking cover. Read the back, didn't sound too interesting, but noticed a quote from Terry Brooks which made me consider it. I picked it up and put it back down a couple of times</span>
  <span id="freeText4167090350452240387" style="display:none">So this book was a pleasant surprise! I left for New York and had only packed one book, thinking I wouldn't be able to read the entire book on my trip...oops. So I had to run to the bookstore to pick out another book to read. The bookstore closed in five minuets and I quickly grabbed the book because of it's interesting looking cover. Read the back, didn't sound too interesting, but noticed a quote from Terry Brooks which made me consider it. I picked it up and put it back down a couple of times, until the store said they were closed and I needed to hurry. I grabbed the book and thought what the heck, I'll give it a go. Read the first part, it was pretty good but not amazing. All of the sudden, out of nowhere, the book is insanely good and I am freaking out in the plane wanting to talk to someone about what's happening. I highly recommend this book and am happy I have found a new addicting series. <br /><br />First read 1/21/09<br />Second read 12/4/12</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15877485773759600540"><b>“Assassination is an art, milord. And I am the city's most accomplished artist.” <br/>― Brent Weeks, The Way of Shadows</b><br/><br/><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/>The story starts out with a bang, and the author has built just enough mystery around the main characters and their motives to keep me turning the pages. The book is busy, it's fast moving, but I found it sometimes to be more complex than it needs be. I just hope it gets better in the following books.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1073797221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1073797221" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513342355p2/8409451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1073797221?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8409451-kristen?shelf=fantasy-is-my-jam">fantasy-is-my-jam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8409451-kristen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8409451-kristen?shelf=favorite-reads-of-2015">favorite-reads-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1073797221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13603995882737179681"><br/>5/5 stars<br/><br/><i>“Killing was no longer an activity, it was a state of being. Kylar <b>became</b> killing.”</i><br/><br/><b>The Skinny:</b><br/><br/>This story follows Azoth as he becomes the wetboy, Kylar Stern. Under the tutelage of Durzo Blint, Kylar slowly transforms into one of the most formidable wetboys in the city. Kylar’s is put to the test, both physically and mentally, when a force larger than he could have anticipated threatens his city. <br/><br/><b>My Review:</b><br/><br/>As far as Fantasy goes, this is not the best out there. The politics were so-so, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13603995882737179681" style="display:none"><br>5/5 stars<br><br><i>“Killing was no longer an activity, it was a state of being. Kylar <b>became</b> killing.”</i><br><br><b>The Skinny:</b><br><br>This story follows Azoth as he becomes the wetboy, Kylar Stern. Under the tutelage of Durzo Blint, Kylar slowly transforms into one of the most formidable wetboys in the city. Kylar’s is put to the test, both physically and mentally, when a force larger than he could have anticipated threatens his city. <br><br><b>My Review:</b><br><br>As far as Fantasy goes, this is not the best out there. The politics were so-so, and the writing, at times, was basic, almost YA feeling (but the violence was most definitely NOT YA). When I think of a good political fantasy that also has that court intrigue/conspiracy, I think of The Goblin Emperor. This was no Goblin Emperor. Yet…<br><br><b>I don’t fucking care - I loved the entire goddam book!</b><br><br><a href="http://s871.photobucket.com/user/Kwagz1/media/Gifs/haters-gonna-hate-scooter1_zps35706c06.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431004743ra/14786157.gif" alt="Haters Gonna Hate photo haters-gonna-hate-scooter1_zps35706c06.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m not lying when I tell you that I was on the edge of my seat for the majority of this read. The villains were so…VILLAINOUS! Rat, a foe from Kylar’s earlier years, was the most hideous of characters. He reminded me of Ramsay Bolton from GOT (the show). He is really just a sick, sick character with no moral compass. Similarly, Roth, another weasel, was also on my “to-die” list. Roth is basically a bastard in nice clothing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I know I am talking about Rat and Roth as if they are two different people here…I don’t want to give anything away, okay!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://s871.photobucket.com/user/Kwagz1/media/Gifs/choke.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440699300ra/16011950.gif" alt="G Dragon Choking Someone photo choke.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>On the flip side, there were several refreshingly kind characters, namely: Logan, Drake, and Doll Girl. There were also many characters (Momma K) that seemed to walk the thinnest of lines between good and evil. At times, these characters had me both loving and hating them. I was such a see-saw of emotions.<br><br>I loved reading about the internal struggle that Kylar goes through as he transitions from Azoth to Kylar. He is a good person at heart, yet wants what most people want: to be strong and unafraid. Because of his innate goodness, Kylar is constantly facing an internal battle. <br><br>The most complex character was probably Durzo himself. He was such a vivid tangle of feelings and emotions. It was obvious that Durzo wanted to not care about life, nor himself, but that it was impossible for him. Despite trying to distance himself, Durzo was connected to several people by such a delicate strand of love. No matter how hard he tried, it was impossible for Durzo to sever the thread.<br><br>This book had my heart-a-poundin for virtually the entire second half of the book. Nothing was ever as it seemed. The numerous ‘reveals’ and plot-twists were devastating and most were surprising. There were a couple that I had guessed from pretty early on, but the majority knocked me on my ass. I was also blown away by some of the fight scenes. Not only were they pretty brutal, but they also 100% kicked ass. <br><br>**I had this pretty little list all prepared of all the reasons why I enjoyed reading this book. As you can tell from this review, the pretty little list went out the window. Instead, you get a muddled review, half fan-girl, have nonsense…you’re welcome?<br><br><br><b>Overall:</b><br><br>I need the next book. NOW.<br><br><a href="http://s871.photobucket.com/user/Kwagz1/media/Gifs/DOWANT.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433724893ra/15135357.gif" alt="Do you Want? photo DOWANT.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_167621039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167621039" />
    <a title="Nimrod Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5175502-nimrod-daniel"><img alt="Nimrod Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344358412p2/5175502.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167621039?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nimrod Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nimrod Daniel" href="/user/show/5175502-nimrod-daniel">Nimrod Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6070107-the-way-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5175502-nimrod-daniel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167621039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13290527053893906497">The way of Shadows had been waiting for me to read for a very long time, and I’m glad I finally got around it. It’s a gritty coming of age story that has a great cast of characters and an intricate plot. While it has a few minor flaws it’s a fantastic debut by Brent Weeks.<br/><br/>The characters are really well-drawn and most of them are very compelling. I liked the two main characters Durzo and Kyler, who are actually anti-heroes. Momma K, Solom, Dorian are really great charcters as well and I liked the</span>
  <span id="freeText13290527053893906497" style="display:none">The way of Shadows had been waiting for me to read for a very long time, and I’m glad I finally got around it. It’s a gritty coming of age story that has a great cast of characters and an intricate plot. While it has a few minor flaws it’s a fantastic debut by Brent Weeks.<br /><br />The characters are really well-drawn and most of them are very compelling. I liked the two main characters Durzo and Kyler, who are actually anti-heroes. Momma K, Solom, Dorian are really great charcters as well and I liked them too. I also cared for a few supporting characters like Logan and Ellene and found both of them pretty good as supporting characters.<br /><br />The world and the magic system are very intriguing. The mechanism and limitations of the magic system feels somewhat vague, but I have no problem with that. The plot focuses on a small region so there's a lot to explore in the following books and learn more about other places and their history. <br /><br />The intricate plot is really great and very captivating with a few interesting twists that will keep you on the edge. Having said that, I had some reservations regarding the way a few things were pulled-off, mainly for the way they were written, not the ideas themselves, but it’s forgivable considering it was Brent’s debut. Even though I really liked the book I didn’t feel like “I must read more now”, but that's ok. <br /><br />All in all, it’s a very good fantasy novel. <br /><br />4.25-4.5/5 (the ending pulls it more towards 4.5)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13290527053893906497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_85371220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85371220" />
    <a title="Nate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2632107-nate"><img alt="Nate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427656792p2/2632107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85371220?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate" href="/user/show/2632107-nate">Nate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2632107-nate?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85371220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer596247559716621828">A somewhat awful page-turner:<br/><br/>A page-turner I'm embarrassed to have finished. The plot in this exciting thriller rolls along, almost too swiftly, but ultimately left me unfulfilled. The author never fleshes out his world or the characters inhabiting it. They often lack motivation for their actions and are little more than mere vehicles for the plot, whose elements fit *too well* together. The central love story is so trite its laugh-out-loud funny, and while I realize Mr. Weeks met his wife at a </span>
  <span id="freeText596247559716621828" style="display:none">A somewhat awful page-turner:<br /><br />A page-turner I'm embarrassed to have finished. The plot in this exciting thriller rolls along, almost too swiftly, but ultimately left me unfulfilled. The author never fleshes out his world or the characters inhabiting it. They often lack motivation for their actions and are little more than mere vehicles for the plot, whose elements fit *too well* together. The central love story is so trite its laugh-out-loud funny, and while I realize Mr. Weeks met his wife at a very young age, we'd need a little more explanation for our hero's affection for a girl than that they knew each other when they were young. This element ruined the ending for me, and Weeks showed absolutely no capability of handling complex emotions. The book reads like a role-playing game with very maudlin moments thrown in to give it a depth which is beyond this author's reach.<br /><br />This is one of those books where everything falls into place nicely, the characters find out what they need to find out at exactly the precise time for the plot to progress, and every single character introduced ends up being central to the plot if not biologically related to the other characters.<br /><br />I will say there were a few wonderful scenes, especially in the first half, but Weeks needs to learn to linger, slow down, and build these scenes up for a greater payoff. We're barely ever asked to consider something momentous before rushed along to the next bright, shiny plot-object.<br /><br />Very similar to Mistborn in its strengths and weaknesses, but much worse. The hype surrounding this debut obscures what a petty project it is, and while there are some great authors out there, I hope this sort of trilogy isn't indicative of the direction in which the fantasy genre is moving.<br /><br />Read only if you want a *very* light, fun fantasy that clunks along at times but keeps you turning pages and rolling your eyes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="596247559716621828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
